Razi's Acceptance of the Mu'tazila Meaning
Razi accepts the Mu'tazila meaning and states the real point of disagreement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Razi accepts the Mu'tazila meaning of mutakallim and identifies the true point of disagreement with them.

Core Idea
The Ash'ari-Mu'tazila dispute is about an additional eternal speech, not the meaning of mutakallim.

Razi concludes the discussion by clarifying his position. He does not reject the Mu'tazila meaning of mutakallim; rather, he accepts it. The real issue is whether there is an additional eternal speech beyond that. This passage sets the stage for the Ash'ari positive doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read Razi's statement about the Mu'tazila meaning of mutakallim. Notice how he explicitly says he does not deny it.
He uses 'نقول به ونعترف به' (we assert and acknowledge).
2
Identify the point of disagreement
Find where Razi states the only disagreement: we affirm an additional thing (أمر آخر) beyond the Mu'tazila meaning, and they deny it.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this distinction matters. It shows that the debate is not about whether Allah speaks in a general sense, but about the nature of that speech.
This leads to the Ash'ari doctrine of eternal speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فثبت بما ذكرنا أن كونه تعالى متكلما بالمعنى الذي يقوله المعتزلة مما نقول به ونعترف به ولا ننكره بوجه من الوجوه، إنما الخلاف بيننا وبينهم في أنا نثبت أمرًا آخر وراء ذلك، وهم ينكرونه، وسنذكر أن ذلك الشيء ما هو؟ وأما الكرامية فهم يقولون : إنه تعالى يخلق الأصوات والحروف في ذاته وهذا يرجع إلى أنه تعالى هل يجوز أن يكون محلا للحوادث أم لا؟ وأما أصحابنا فقد قالوا : ثبت أن الكلام القائم بالنفس معنى مغاير للقدر والإرادات والعلوم والاعتقادات وندعي أن الباري تعالى موصوف بهذا المعنى، وندعي أن هذا المعنى قديم وندعي أنه معنى واحد وهو مع كونه واحدًا أمر ونهي وخبر واستخبار ونداء.
It is established by what we mentioned that His being mutakallim in the meaning that the Mu'tazila say is something we assert and acknowledge and do not deny in any way. The only disagreement between us and them is that we affirm another thing beyond that, and they deny it. We will mention what that thing is.
As for the Karramiyya, they say: He creates sounds and letters in His essence (dhāt), and this reduces to the question: is it permissible for Him to be a locus for temporal events (maḥall li al-ḥawādith) or not?
As for our companions (Ash'aris), they said: It is established that the speech subsisting in the self (al-kalām al-qā'im bi al-nafs) is a meaning distinct from power, wills, sciences, and beliefs. And we claim that the Creator, Exalted, is described by this meaning. And we claim that this meaning is eternal (qadīm). And we claim that it is one meaning, and while being one, it is command, prohibition, report, inquiry, and call.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage presents Razi's conclusion and the positive Ash'ari doctrine. First, Razi states that he accepts the Mu'tazila meaning of mutakallim—that Allah creates sounds in a body to indicate His will. The real disagreement is that the Ash'aris affirm an additional thing beyond that: an eternal speech subsisting in the self (kalām nafsī). Razi then mentions the Karramiyya view: Allah creates sounds in His own essence, which raises the issue of whether Allah can be a locus for temporal events (ḥawādith). Finally, he summarizes the Ash'ari position: there is a speech subsisting in the self that is distinct from power, wills, sciences, and beliefs; it is eternal; it is one meaning; and despite being one, it encompasses command, prohibition, report, inquiry, and call. This is the established Ash'ari doctrine of kalām nafsī.

Key Terms
متكلم
معتزلة
أمر آخر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Razi completely rejects the Mu'tazila view on divine speech.
Correction: Razi explicitly accepts the Mu'tazila meaning of mutakallim and only adds an additional eternal speech.

Checkpoint
What does Razi say about the Mu'tazila meaning of mutakallim?
A) He rejects it completely.
B) He accepts it and does not deny it.
C) He is indifferent.
D) He only partially accepts it.

Key Takeaway
Razi accepts the Mu'tazila meaning of mutakallim and clarifies that the real debate is about affirming an eternal speech beyond it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter differing Islamic views, do you instinctively focus on the disagreements or first acknowledge areas of common ground like Razi did? Can you honestly say you separate secondary differences from primary ones in your own heart?
?
Razi affirms that Allah creates sounds to speak, but insists there is an eternal speech beyond that. Do you treat the Quran as merely a temporal creation, or do you truly believe it is the eternal word of Allah? What difference does that belief make in how you recite and listen to it?
?
If you were to dialogue with a Mu'tazili today, would you be able to clearly state where you agree and where you disagree, as Razi did? Or would you let the disagreement overshadow the common ground? What does that reveal about your intention: to win an argument or to seek truth?

The Karramiyya View and the Ash'ari Doctrine of Eternal Speech
Razi presents the Karramiyya view and summarizes the Ash'ari positive doctrine of kalām nafsī.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Karramiyya view on divine speech and the Ash'ari doctrine of eternal speech subsisting in the self.

Core Idea
The Ash'ari kalām nafsī is an eternal, single meaning that encompasses all forms of speech.

After stating his acceptance of the Mu'tazila meaning, Razi turns to the Karramiyya, who hold a different view about sounds in Allah's essence. He then presents the full Ash'ari positive doctrine: an eternal speech that is one yet multiple. This passage is the heart of the Ash'ari position on the attribute of speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the Karramiyya view
Find what the Karramiyya say about divine speech: they claim Allah creates sounds and letters in His own essence (ذاته).
This is distinct from the Mu'tazila view, where sounds are created in a body outside Allah.
2
Understand the issue of 'locus for temporal events'
Razi points out that this view raises the question of whether Allah can be a locus for temporal events (محل للحوادث). Consider why this is problematic.
Ash'aris reject that Allah can be a locus for accidents.
3
Read the Ash'ari doctrine
Read the three claims: (1) speech subsisting in the self is a distinct meaning, (2) it is eternal, (3) it is one yet encompasses command, prohibition, etc.
Notice the emphasis on 'one meaning' despite multiple manifestations.
4
Reflect on the unity of kalām nafsī
Consider how a single meaning can be command, prohibition, report, inquiry, and call. This is a key Ash'ari concept.
Think of it as a single attribute with multiple relations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فثبت بما ذكرنا أن كونه تعالى متكلما بالمعنى الذي يقوله المعتزلة مما نقول به ونعترف به ولا ننكره بوجه من الوجوه، إنما الخلاف بيننا وبينهم في أنا نثبت أمرًا آخر وراء ذلك، وهم ينكرونه، وسنذكر أن ذلك الشيء ما هو؟ وأما الكرامية فهم يقولون : إنه تعالى يخلق الأصوات والحروف في ذاته وهذا يرجع إلى أنه تعالى هل يجوز أن يكون محلا للحوادث أم لا؟ وأما أصحابنا فقد قالوا : ثبت أن الكلام القائم بالنفس معنى مغاير للقدر والإرادات والعلوم والاعتقادات وندعي أن الباري تعالى موصوف بهذا المعنى، وندعي أن هذا المعنى قديم وندعي أنه معنى واحد وهو مع كونه واحدًا أمر ونهي وخبر واستخبار ونداء.
It is established by what we mentioned that His being mutakallim in the meaning that the Mu'tazila say is something we assert and acknowledge and do not deny in any way. The only disagreement between us and them is that we affirm another thing beyond that, and they deny it. We will mention what that thing is.
As for the Karramiyya, they say: He creates sounds and letters in His essence (dhāt), and this reduces to the question: is it permissible for Him to be a locus for temporal events (maḥall li al-ḥawādith) or not?
As for our companions (Ash'aris), they said: It is established that the speech subsisting in the self (al-kalām al-qā'im bi al-nafs) is a meaning distinct from power, wills, sciences, and beliefs. And we claim that the Creator, Exalted, is described by this meaning. And we claim that this meaning is eternal (qadīm). And we claim that it is one meaning, and while being one, it is command, prohibition, report, inquiry, and call.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage presents Razi's conclusion and the positive Ash'ari doctrine. First, Razi states that he accepts the Mu'tazila meaning of mutakallim—that Allah creates sounds in a body to indicate His will. The real disagreement is that the Ash'aris affirm an additional thing beyond that: an eternal speech subsisting in the self (kalām nafsī). Razi then mentions the Karramiyya view: Allah creates sounds in His own essence, which raises the issue of whether Allah can be a locus for temporal events (ḥawādith). Finally, he summarizes the Ash'ari position: there is a speech subsisting in the self that is distinct from power, wills, sciences, and beliefs; it is eternal; it is one meaning; and despite being one, it encompasses command, prohibition, report, inquiry, and call. This is the established Ash'ari doctrine of kalām nafsī.

قديم
أمر
نهي

استخبار
نداء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Eternal speech is multiple because it includes command, prohibition, etc.
Correction: The Ash'aris hold that it is one meaning that encompasses these aspects without being multiple.

Checkpoint
What is the Karramiyya view on divine speech?
A) Allah creates sounds in a body other than Himself.
B) Allah creates sounds in His own essence.
C) Allah does not speak.
D) Allah's speech is eternal.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari doctrine affirms an eternal, single speech subsisting in the self that is distinct from all other attributes and encompasses command, prohibition, report, inquiry, and call.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's speech is one eternal meaning, how does that unify your understanding of every verse you recite? Will you read the Qur'an today as if each word is part of one timeless address to you?
?
The Karramiyya imagined Allah creating sounds in Himself—do you ever imagine that Allah's speech is limited to the letters on the page? How does the eternity of His kalām nafsī change the weight you give to His commands and prohibitions?
?
Which of the five manifestations of divine speech—command, prohibition, report, inquiry, call—do you most avoid responding to in your daily life? Commit to answering one of them concretely before this day ends.

Proof That God Has Internal Speech
Razi proves the second point: God is described with internal speech using evidence from prophets and miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi proves that God possesses internal speech (kalam nafsi) distinct from His will and knowledge, using the evidence of prophetic reports and miracles.

Core Idea
God's commands and reports signify a real meaning beyond His will and knowledge — this is internal speech.

Imam Razi addresses a crucial point in the Ash'ari doctrine: that God's speech is not merely sound or letter, but a real attribute. While the first point (establishing internal speech as a distinct meaning) has been covered, Razi now provides the proof that God actually possesses this attribute. He builds his argument on the undeniable fact that prophets universally reported that God commands, forbids, and informs, and their truthfulness is confirmed by miracles.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two points
Razi divides the discussion into two points: first, showing that internal speech is a distinct meaning; second, proving that God has it. This lesson covers the second point.
The first point is assumed already established.
2
Follow the proof from tawatur
Read how Razi uses the mass transmission (tawatur) of prophetic reports to establish that God commands, forbids, and informs. Miracles confirm the prophets' truthfulness.
3
Analyze the dichotomy of words vs. meanings
Razi argues that these acts (command, prohibition, report) are either mere words or real meanings. If words, they must signify something beyond themselves.
This leads to the conclusion that the signified meaning cannot be God's will or knowledge.
4
Understand why it cannot be will or knowledge
Razi gives the reason: command can exist without will (e.g., a test), and report without belief (e.g., a false statement). So the signified meaning must be something else — internal speech.
This is the core of the Ash'ari argument.
5
Address the circularity objection
Razi anticipates an objection: using prophecy to prove God's speech presupposes knowledge that God speaks. He refutes it by noting that miracles independently confirm prophethood, so no circularity.
This preserves the logical order of evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما المقام الأول وهو إثبات أن كلام النفس أمر مغاير للإرادات والاعتقادات فقد تقدم تقريره على أحسن الوجوه. وأما المقام الثاني وهو أن الباري تعالى موصوف بكلام النفس فالذي يدل عليه ما ثبت عندنا بالتواتر الظاهر من جميع الأنبياء والرسل صلى الله عليهم وسلم أنه تعالى أمر عباده بكذا ونهاهم عن كذا وأخبرهم بكذا ولما ثبت بالمعجزات صدق الأنبياء والرسل صلى الله عليهم وسلم وجب القطع بكونه تعالى أمرًا وناهيًا ومخيرًا. وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول هذا الأمر والنهي والخبر إما أن يكون من باب الألفاظ والعبارات وإما أن يكون من باب المعاني والحقائق فإن كان الأول فتلك العبارات والألفاظ لا بد وأن تكون دالة على المعاني والمدلولات فمدلول هذه العبارات في حق الله تعالى إما أن يكون هو الإرادات والاعتقادات وإما أن يكون معنى مغايرا لها لا جائز أن تكون تلك المعاني هي الإرادات والاعتقادات لأنا بينا أن الأمر قد يوجد بدون الإرادة والخبر قد يوجد بدون الاعتقادات. فثبت أن مدلول هذه العبارة في حق الله تعالى معنى وراء الاعتقادات والإرادات فثبت أنه تعالى موصوف بمعنى حقيقي وهو مدلول قوله افعل وهو مغاير لإرادته وأنه تعالى موصوف بمعنى حقيقي هو مدلول قوله الحمد لله وهو مغاير لعلمه ونحن نسمي ذلك المعنى بالأمر الحقيقي والخبر الحقيقي وهو المطلوب. فإن قيل كيف يمكنكم أن تستدلوا بقول الأنبياء والرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام على كونه تعالى متكلما مع أن نبوة الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام لا يمكن إثباتها إلا بعد العلم بكونه تعالى متكلما قلنا لا نسلم أن العلم بصحة نبوة الأنبياء موقوف على العلم بكونه تعالى متكلما وذلك لأنه لما ظهرت المعجزات على وفق دعاويهم ثبت كونهم صادقين سواء علمنا كونه تعالى متكلما أو لم نعلم ذلك.
As for the first point—which is the proof that internal speech (kalam nafsi) is a meaning different from wills and beliefs—its explanation has already been presented in the best manner. As for the second point—which is that the Creator, exalted, is described with internal speech—what indicates it is what has been established for us by manifest tawatur (mass transmission) from all the prophets and messengers, peace be upon them, that He, exalted, commanded His servants thus, forbade them thus, and informed them thus. When the truthfulness of the prophets and messengers, peace be upon them, was established by miracles, it became necessary to be certain that He, exalted, is commanding, forbidding, and informing. When this is established, we say: This command, prohibition, and report are either in the category of words and expressions, or in the category of meanings and realities. If the first, then those expressions and words must indicate meanings and signifieds. The signified of these expressions with respect to God, exalted, is either wills and beliefs or a meaning different from them. It is not possible that those meanings be wills and beliefs, because we have explained that command may exist without will, and report may exist without beliefs. Thus it is established that the signified of this expression with respect to God, exalted, is a meaning beyond beliefs and wills. Thus it is established that He, exalted, is described with a real meaning, which is the signified of His saying 'Do', and it is different from His will; and that He, exalted, is described with a real meaning which is the signified of His saying 'Praise be to Allah', and it is different from His knowledge. We call that meaning 'real command' and 'real report', and that is what is sought. If it is said: How can you use the statements of the prophets and messengers, peace be upon them, to prove that He, exalted, is mutakallim, given that the prophethood of the prophets, peace be upon them, cannot be established except after knowing that He, exalted, is mutakallim? We say: We do not concede that knowledge of the validity of the prophethood of the prophets is dependent on knowledge that He, exalted, is mutakallim, because when the miracles appeared in accordance with their claims, their truthfulness was established, whether we know that He, exalted, is mutakallim or we do not know that.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a proof (istidlal) for the second of the four disputed points: that God is described with internal speech (kalam nafsi). Razi begins by noting that the first point—that internal speech is a distinct meaning—has already been established. He then provides the proof for the second point. The proof relies on the widespread and continuous reports (tawatur) from all prophets that God commanded, forbade, and informed. Since the truth of the prophets is confirmed by miracles, we are certain that God truly commands, forbids, and informs. Now, these acts of commanding, forbidding, and informing are either mere words/sounds or are real meanings. If they are mere words, those words must signify something. What they signify cannot be God's will or knowledge, because it is possible for a command to exist without the commander genuinely willing the action (e.g., a test), and for a report to be given without the reporter believing it (e.g., a false report). Therefore, what is signified by God's words must be a meaning distinct from His will and knowledge. This meaning is what the Ash'aris call 'real command' and 'real report'—i.e., internal speech. Razi then addresses an objection: How can we use the prophets' statements to prove that God speaks, when prophethood itself requires knowing that God speaks? The objection implies a circular dependence. Razi refutes it by arguing that prophecy is established by miracles, which do not require prior knowledge of God's speech. Miracles confirm the truthfulness of the prophets independently. Thus, from their truthful reports we can infer that God is mutakallim with internal speech. This rebuttal preserves the logical order of evidence.

Key Terms
كلام النفس (kalam nafsi)
تواتر (tawatur)
معجزة (miracle)
أمر حقيقي (real command)
خبر حقيقي (real report)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof is circular: you need to know God speaks to accept prophecy, but you use prophecy to prove God speaks.
Correction: Razi shows that miracles independently establish the truthfulness of prophets, so no prior knowledge of God's speech is needed. The proof is valid.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, why can't the meanings signified by God's commands and reports be His will or knowledge?
A) Because will and knowledge are not meanings.
B) Because command can exist without will, and report without belief.
C) Because God's will and knowledge are not real.
D) Because the prophets said so.

Key Takeaway
Internal speech is the real meaning of God's commands and reports, distinct from His will and knowledge, proven through the testimony of prophets confirmed by miracles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear the command 'Do not commit injustice,' do you experience it as a mere word or as a real meaning that obligates you? What would change in your heart if you truly believed that command is an eternal, real attribute in God's essence, not just a reflection of His will? Will you obey it as an absolute demand or as a suggestion you can negotiate?
?
Razi says a command can exist without the commander's will. Think of a time you obeyed a command you did not want to obey. Did that obedience still hold weight? Now, how does that affect your view of God's commands that conflict with your desires? Are you willing to obey even when your will resists, because the command itself is a real meaning from God?
?
If God's internal speech is distinct from His knowledge, then His commands are not merely informative advice—they are authoritative directives. Which command of God are you currently treating as merely informational rather than binding? What step will you take today to submit to that command as a real, personal address from your Lord?

Divine Attributes

8 min
Proving God's Inner Speech as a Real Attribute Distinct from Will and Knowledge
Razi proves God's inner speech via tawatur and logical analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses the tawatur of prophets and logical analysis to establish that God's speech is a real meaning (inner speech) distinct from His will and knowledge.

Core Idea
God's speech is not sounds but a real eternal attribute proven by tawatur and rational necessity.

Razi presents a sophisticated argument that God's commands, prohibitions, and news must be real meanings, not mere words or expressions. He begins with the established testimony of prophets, confirmed by miracles, and then analyzes the nature of these divine acts to conclude that they point to an inner attribute of speech that is distinct from will and knowledge. This passage also addresses a potential circularity objection.

Guided Path
1
Understand the tawatur foundation
Read the opening where Razi cites the unanimous testimony of all prophets that God commands, prohibits, and informs. Recognize that miracles confirm their truthfulness, so we know God is a commander, prohibitor, and informer.
Tawatur means widely transmitted, giving certainty.
2
Follow the disjunction
Notice that Razi divides these divine acts into either words/expressions or meanings/reals. The first option leads to a necessary signification.
3
See why signification is not will or knowledge
Razi argues that command can exist without will and news without belief. Therefore, the meaning signified must be something else—a distinct attribute called inner speech.
Think of a test command or a lie to grasp this.
4
Appreciate the real command and real news
He specifies that the command 'Do' signifies a meaning distinct from will, and the news 'Praise be to God' signifies a meaning distinct from knowledge. This meaning is what we call real command and real news.
5
Examine the objection and response
Razi answers the charge of circularity: prophethood is proven by miracles, not prior knowledge of God's speech, so the argument stands.
This shows the strength of the proof from miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المقام الثاني : وهو أن الباري تعالى موصوف بكلام النفس، فالذي يدل عليه ما ثبت عندنا بالتواتر الظاهر من جميع الأنبياء والرسل - صلى الله عليهم وسلم - أنه تعالى أمر عباده بكذا ونهاهم عن كذا وأخبرهم بكذا ، ولما ثبت بالمعجزات صدق الأنبياء والرسل - صلى الله عليهم وسلم - وجب القطع بكونه تعالى أمرًا وناهيا ومخيرًا. وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : هذا الأمر والنهي والخبر إما أن يكون من باب الألفاظ والعبارات، وإما أن يكون من باب المعاني والحقائق، فإن كان الأول، فتلك العبارات والألفاظ لا بد وأن تكون دالة على المعاني والمدلولات فمدلول هذه العبارات في حق الله تعالى إما أن يكون هو الإرادات والاعتقادات، وإما أن يكون معنى مغايرا لها . لا جائز أن تكون تلك المعاني هي الإرادات والاعتقادات؛ لأنا بينا أن الأمر قد يوجد بدون الإرادة والخبر قد يوجد بدون الاعتقادات. فثبت أن مدلول هذه العبارة في حق الله تعالى معنى وراء الاعتقادات ،والأرادات فثبت أنه تعالى موصوف بمعنى حقيقي، وهو مدلول قوله : "افعل"، وهو مغاير لإرادته، وأنه تعالى موصوف بمعنى حقيقي هو مدلول قوله : الحمد لله، وهو مغاير لعلمه، ونحن نسمي ذلك المعنى بالأمر الحقيقي والخبر الحقيقي وهو المطلوب. فإن قيل : كيف يمكنكم أن تستدلوا بقول الأنبياء والرسل - عليهم الصلاة والسلام - على كونه تعالى متكلما مع أن نبوة الأنبياء - عليهم الصلاة والسلام - لا يمكن إثباتها إلا بعد العلم بكونه تعالى متكلما . قلنا : لا نسلم أن العلم بصحة نبوة الأنبياء موقوف على العلم بكونه تعالى متكلما ، وذلك لأنه لما ظهرت المعجزات على وفق دعاويهم، ثبت كونهم صادقين سواء علمنا كونه تعالى متكلما أو لم نعلم ذلك.
As for the second station—that the Exalted Creator is described with inner speech—what indicates it is what is established for us by manifest tawatur from all the prophets and messengers (peace be upon them): that He, exalted, commanded His servants such-and-such, prohibited them from such-and-such, and informed them of such-and-such. And since the truthfulness of the prophets and messengers (peace be upon them) has been established by miracles, it is necessary to be certain that He, exalted, is a commander, a prohibitor, and an informer. If this is established, we say: this command, prohibition, and news are either of the category of words and expressions, or of the category of meanings and realities. If the first, then those expressions and words must indicate meanings and significations. The signification of these expressions with respect to God, exalted, is either wills and beliefs, or a meaning distinct from them. It is not possible that those meanings are wills and beliefs, because we have explained that command can exist without will and news can exist without beliefs. Thus it is established that the signification of this expression with respect to God, exalted, is a meaning beyond beliefs and wills. So it is established that He, exalted, is described with a real meaning, which is the signification of His saying "Do" (if‘al), and it is distinct from His will; and that He, exalted, is described with a real meaning which is the signification of His saying "Praise be to God" (al-hamdu lillah), and it is distinct from His knowledge. We call that meaning the real command and the real news, and that is the desired conclusion. If it is said: How can you argue from the sayings of the prophets and messengers (peace be upon them) that He, exalted, is speaking, given that the prophethood of the prophets (peace be upon them) cannot be established except after knowing that He, exalted, is speaking? We say: We do not concede that knowledge of the validity of the prophets' prophethood is dependent on knowledge that He, exalted, is speaking. This is because when miracles appeared in accordance with their claims, they are established as truthful whether we know that He, exalted, is speaking or we do not know that.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a proof that God is described with inner speech. Razi begins by citing the unanimous testimony of the prophets (tawatur) that God commands, prohibits, and informs. Since the prophets are confirmed by miracles, we know that God is a commander, prohibitor, and informer. Then Razi analyzes the nature of these divine acts: they are either mere words (alfaz) or real meanings (ma'ani). If they are words, those words must signify something. The signification cannot be God's will or knowledge, because a command can exist without will (e.g., a test) and news can exist without belief (e.g., a lie). Therefore, the signification must be a distinct meaning—this is inner speech. Specifically, the command 'Do' signifies a meaning distinct from will, and the news 'Praise be to God' signifies a meaning distinct from knowledge. Razi then addresses an objection: how can you prove God is speaking from the prophets when prophethood itself requires knowing God speaks? He replies that prophethood is proven by miracles, which do not require prior knowledge that God speaks. Thus the argument is not circular.

Key Terms
كلام النفس
الأمر الحقيقي
الخبر الحقيقي
تواتر
معجزات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that God's speech is merely created sounds or letters.
Correction: Razi argues that speech is a real meaning (inner speech) that is eternal and distinct from will and knowledge, not contingent sounds.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, what is the key reason that the signification of God's commands and news cannot be His will or knowledge?
A) Because will and knowledge are eternal, while commands are temporal.
B) Because command can exist without will and news without belief.
C) Because God's will is identical to His knowledge.
D) Because the prophets did not mention will or knowledge.

Key Takeaway
God's inner speech is a real, distinct attribute proven by prophetic testimony and rational analysis, not reducible to will or knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's command is a real meaning distinct from His will, then His command 'Do not commit sin' is not a mere suggestion but a real, eternal imperative. Do you relate to God's commands as external rules or as a reflection of His eternal speech that demands your entire being?
?
Razi proves that news can exist without belief. Consider the news of the Day of Judgment: you hear it, but does your heart truly believe? In what areas do you treat God's news as mere information rather than a reality that must transform your life?
?
How would your relationship with the Quran change if you truly internalised that its words signify a real, eternal attribute of God? Would you still read it as just guidance or as an encounter with His inner speech?

Proof That Divine Inner Speech Is Eternal
Razi proves the eternity of inner speech via trilemma and reconciles with Mu'tazilite created sounds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's trilemma argument that divine inner speech must be eternal and how he reconciles with the Mu'tazilite position on created sounds.

Core Idea
If God's speech were created, it would have to exist somewhere — but nowhere is possible.

Razi presents a crisp rational argument: divine speech cannot be created because a created attribute would have to inhere in God (making Him temporal) or in another (impossible for an attribute) or nowhere (impossible). Having ruled out creation, he concludes it is eternal. He then addresses the Mu'tazilite objection that God's speech is sounds created in other objects, clarifying that such sounds are expressions of an inner divine attribute that is eternal and subsisting in God.

Guided Path
1
Read the trilemma
Read the passage and identify Razi's three options for a created attribute: inhering in God, inhering in another, or inhering in no locus. Note why each is impossible.
The trilemma forces the conclusion that the attribute cannot be created.
2
Examine the Mu'tazilite concession
Notice that Razi grants that God can create sounds in other objects, as the Mu'tazila claim. This is not the point of dispute.
Razi does not deny the possibility of created sounds; he shifts the focus to what those sounds signify.
3
Understand the proof of inner meaning
Razi argues that created sounds must have significations (inner concepts). Those significations cannot be will or knowledge (as proven earlier), so they must be distinct, eternal attributes subsisting in God.
This establishes the reality of inner speech (kalam nafsi).
4
Grasp the reconciliation
Razi concludes that both the Mu'tazilite position (speech as created sounds) and the Ash'ari position (speech as eternal inner attribute) are correct in their own terms. The dispute is semantic, arising from not clarifying the two meanings of 'speech'.
The lesson is to carefully define terms before arguing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المقام الثالث : وهو أنا ندعي أن هذه الصفة قديمة فنقول : لو كانت محدثة لكانت إما قائمة به أو بغيره أو لا في محل فإن كانت قائمة به كان الله تعالى محلا للحوادث، وهو محال، وإذا كانت قائمة بغيره فهو أيضًا محال، و إن لم تكن قائمة بشيء أو كانت قائمة بغيره أو كانت موجودة لا في غير محل فهو محال؛ لأنا بينا أن هذا الكلام صفة الله تعالى ونعته ومن المحال ان تحصل صفة الشيء ونعته لا فيه بل في غيره والذي يقوله المعتزلة من أنه يجوز أن يكون كلامه قائما بغيره هذا الباب، وذلك لأنهم فسروا الكلام القائم بغيره بأنه يخلق أصواتا و حروفًا دالة بالوضع والاصطلاح على كونه تعالى مريدا لبعض الأشياء وكارها لبعضها، وهذا غير ممتنع البتة. فليس من ذلك وأما نحن في هذا المقام فقد بينا أنه لو خلق ألفاظا دالة على الطلب وألفاظا دالة على الحكم والإسناد فلا بد من مدلولات لتلك الألفاظ ومفهومات، وبينا أن الألفاظ الدالة على الطلب لا يمكن أن يكون مدلولها الإرادة والألفاظ الدالة على الخبر لا يمكن أن يكون مدلولها العلم، فلا بد من صفات أخرى قائمة بذات الله تعالى، تكون تلك الصفات مدلولة الألفاظ الدالة على الطلب والألفاظ الدالة على الخبر وتلك المدلولات يمتنع كونها مباينة عن ذات الله تعالى بل يجب كونها قائمة بذات الله تعالى. والذي يقوله المعتزلة من يجوز أن يكون الحي متكلما بكلام قائم بالغير حق وصدق، والذي يقوله أصحابنا أنه من يمتنع أن يكون الحي متكلما بكلام قائم بالغير حق وصدق، إلا أن الكلام الذي يشير إليه المعتزلة له معنى، والكلام الذي يشير إليه أصحابنا، له معنى آخر والفرقان لما لم يشتغلوا بتلخيص محل النزاع لا جرم خفيت هذه المباحث والمطالب.
As for the third station—that we claim this attribute is eternal—we say: if it were originated (muhdatha), then either it would subsist in Him, or in another, or in no locus. If it subsists in Him, then God, exalted, would be a locus for originated things, which is impossible. If it subsists in another, that also is impossible. If it does not subsist in anything, or if it subsists in another, or if it exists without a locus, that is impossible; because we have explained that this speech is an attribute of God, exalted, and His description, and it is impossible for an attribute and description of a thing to occur not in it but in another. As for what the Mu'tazila say—that it is permissible for His speech to subsist in another—this is their position, because they interpret speech subsisting in another as His creating sounds and letters which, by convention and terminology, indicate that He, exalted, wills some things and dislikes others. This is not impossible at all. That is not the case. As for us in this station, we have explained that if He created words indicating request and words indicating judgment and attribution, then there must be significations (madlulat) and concepts for those words. We have shown that the words indicating request cannot have will as their signification, and the words indicating news cannot have knowledge as their signification. Thus there must be other attributes subsisting in the essence of God, exalted, such that those attributes are the significations of the words indicating request and the words indicating news. Those significations cannot be separate from the essence of God, exalted; rather they must subsist in His essence. What the Mu'tazila say—that it is permissible for a living being to speak with speech subsisting in another—is true and correct, and what our scholars say—that it is impossible for a living being to speak with speech subsisting in another—is true and correct, except that the speech to which the Mu'tazila refer has one meaning, and the speech to which our scholars refer has another meaning. Since they did not bother to summarize the point of dispute, these investigations and demands remained hidden.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a proof that inner speech is eternal. Razi uses a trilemma: if divine speech were originated (created), it must either inhere in God (making Him a locus for temporal events, which is impossible), inhere in another (impossible for an attribute to be in a different substance), or exist without a locus (impossible for an accident). Thus it cannot be originated, so it must be eternal. He then addresses the Mu'tazilite view that God's speech is created sounds subsisting in some other entity (like a tree or angel). Razi concedes that this is not impossible, but argues that such sounds are mere expressions that must signify inner meanings. Those meanings cannot be will or knowledge (as proved earlier), so they must be distinct attributes subsisting in God's essence. Thus both positions (Mu'tazilite created sounds and Ash'arite inner speech) are correct in their own context, but the dispute arises from failing to distinguish the two meanings of 'speech'. Razi concludes that the lack of clarifying the point of dispute hides the truth.

Key Terms
قديم
محدث
قائم بالغير
صفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Ash'ari position denies that God can create sounds in other objects.
Correction: Razi explicitly states that it is not impossible for God to create sounds in other objects; the Ash'ari claim is about the reality of inner speech, not the possibility of created sounds.

Checkpoint
What is the first logical possibility Razi examines for divine speech if it were created?
A) It subsists in God, making Him a locus for temporal events.
B) It subsists in another entity.
C) It exists without a locus.
D) It is identical to God's will.

Key Takeaway
Divine speech consists of two aspects: created sounds (possible) and eternal inner speech (necessary), and the Ash'ari position concerns the latter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you experience it as an eternal attribute of God speaking directly to your soul, or do you treat it as a historical document? What would need to change in your heart to encounter it as the former?
?
Razi argues that God's commands have a reality beyond mere sounds. Are you content with performing outward rituals, or do you seek the inner reality of the command—the eternal speech that demands your obedience today? How can you bridge the gap?
?
The Mu'tazila reduced divine speech to created sounds, while the Ash'aris affirmed an eternal attribute. In your own understanding of God, are you tempted to reduce Him to what you can perceive, or do you allow for attributes that transcend creation? What step can you take this week to deepen your reverence for the uncreated speech of Allah?

Unity of Divine Speech: Command, Prohibition, and News
Razi resolves the apparent multiplicity of divine speech into the single category of news.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that God's speech is one in essence even though it appears as command, prohibition, and news.

Core Idea
All divine speech reduces to news (khabar), preserving its oneness.

In this passage, Imam al-Razi addresses a theological puzzle: how can God's attribute of speech be one if it includes commands, prohibitions, and reports? He resolves this by reducing all forms to a single category—news (khabar). Let's explore his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the key terms: 'amr' (command), 'nahy' (prohibition), and 'khabar' (news).
2
Understand the reduction
Razi argues that command and prohibition are essentially news—they inform the listener about consequences (praise or blame). Grasp this core insight.
3
Connect to oneness
Since all forms of speech are news at root, divine speech is one in reality. Reflect on how this resolves the apparent contradiction.
This is the key takeaway of the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المقام الرابع : وهو أن كلام الله تعالى واحد، ومع كونه وكونه واحدًا فهو أمر ونهي وخبر، فتحقيق الكلام فيه يرجع إلى حرف واحد وهو أن الكلام كله خبر ؛ لأن الأمر عبارة عن تعريف الغير أنه لو فعله لصار مستحقا للمدح، ولو تركه لصار مستحقا للذم وكذا القول في النهي، وإذا كان المرجع بالكل إلى شيء واحد، وهو الخبر صح قولنا : إن كلام الله تعالى واحد فهذا مجموع ما نلخص في هذا الباب.
As for the fourth station—that the speech of God, exalted, is one, and despite being one it is command, prohibition, and news—so the verification of the speech concerning it reduces to a single point: that speech is entirely news (khabar). Because command is an expression for informing another that if he does it, he becomes deserving of praise, and if he abandons it, he becomes deserving of blame; and similarly for prohibition. And when the reference of all is to one thing, which is news, our statement that the speech of God, exalted, is one is correct. This is the total of what we summarize in this chapter.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a resolution of the apparent multiplicity of divine speech. Razi proposes that all forms of divine speech—command, prohibition, and news—can be reduced to a single reality: news (khabar). He argues that a command is essentially an informative statement about the consequence of an action (deserving praise or blame). Prohibition is similar, informing about the consequence of an omission. Therefore, since all types of speech are ultimately informative (khabar), divine speech is one in essence. This allows for the oneness of God's attribute of speech while still acknowledging its diverse expressions.

Key Terms

أمر
نهي
خبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that oneness means God does not command or prohibit.
Correction: Razi explains that oneness is preserved because command and prohibition are subtypes of news, not separate entities.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, to what single category can all types of divine speech be reduced?
A) Command
B) Prohibition
C) News (khabar)
D) Will

Key Takeaway
God's speech is one in reality because all its forms—command, prohibition, and news—are fundamentally informative.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a command from Allah, do you feel burdened by the obligation, or do you recognize it as good news that obedience leads to praise and disobedience to blame? How can you shift your heart from seeing commands as mere rules to seeing them as informative news about the path to success?
?
Razi says that all divine speech is news. If that is true, then every ayah in the Qur'an is a piece of information about reality. How does this change the way you read a verse of law compared to a verse of story? Are you reading them both as equally true news?
?
If prohibition is also news—informing you that doing a certain thing leads to blame—does that make it easier to avoid sin? How can you use this understanding to strengthen your taqwa when you face a temptation?

Razi's Proof of the Eternality of God's Speech
Razi argues that God's speech is eternal by eliminating temporal possibilities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi proves the eternality of God's speech by eliminating all temporal possibilities and how he distinguishes his position from the Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
God's speech is eternal because it cannot be temporal in any mode of subsistence.

In this passage, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi presents a rigorous logical proof for the eternality of God's speech (kalam). He begins by stating his claim and then proceeds by disjunction: if speech were temporal, it would have to exist in one of three ways—in God, in another, or not in a locus. He refutes each possibility. Then he addresses the Mu'tazila view that speech can be created and subsist in another, and clarifies that the real dispute is about the meaning or concept (madlul) of speech, which must be an eternal attribute in God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then read the literal translation to grasp the argument's flow.
Notice the logical disjunction: 'If temporal, then either ... or ... or ...'
2
Identify the disjunctive argument
Razi lists three possibilities for a temporal speech: subsisting in God, in another, or not in a locus. Each is refuted. Follow the refutation logic.
The refutation of 'subsisting in God' relies on the impossibility of God being a locus for temporal events.
3
Understand the Mu'tazila position
Razi explains that the Mu'tazila allow speech to subsist in another, interpreting it as created sounds and letters indicating God's will. He accepts this as not impossible.
This is crucial: Razi does not deny created speech; he distinguishes it from the eternal attribute.
4
Grasp the resolution
Razi explains that if God creates words, they must have meanings. Those meanings cannot be will or knowledge, so they must be other attributes in God. Thus, eternal speech is the meaning, not the created sounds.
The dispute arose because both sides were talking about different things: one about created speech, the other about the eternal attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المقام الثالث : وهو أنا ندعي أن هذه الصفة قديمة فنقول : لو كانت محدثة لكانت إما قائمة به أو بغيره أو لا في محل فإن كانت قائمة به كان الله تعالى محلا للحوادث، وهو محال، وإذا كانت قائمة بغيره فهو أيضًا محال، و إن لم تكن قائمة بشيء أو كانت قائمة بغيره أو كانت موجودة لا في غير محل فهو محال؛ لأنا بينا أن هذا الكلام صفة الله تعالى ونعته ومن المحال ان تحصل صفة الشيء ونعته لا فيه بل في غيره والذي يقوله المعتزلة من أنه يجوز أن يكون كلامه قائما بغيره هذا الباب، وذلك لأنهم فسروا الكلام القائم بغيره بأنه يخلق أصواتا و حروفًا دالة بالوضع والاصطلاح على كونه تعالى مريدا لبعض الأشياء وكارها لبعضها، وهذا غير ممتنع البتة. فليس من وأما نحن في هذا المقام فقد بينا أنه لو خلق ألفاظا دالة على الطلب وألفاظا دالة على الحكم والإسناد فلا بد من مدلولات لتلك الألفاظ ومفهومات، وبينا أن الألفاظ الدالة على الطلب لا يمكن أن يكون مدلولها الإرادة والألفاظ الدالة على الخبر لا يمكن أن يكون مدلولها العلم، فلا بد من صفات أخرى قائمة بذات الله تعالى، تكون تلك الصفات مدلولة الألفاظ الدالة على الطلب والألفاظ الدالة على الخبر وتلك المدلولات يمتنع كونها مباينة عن ذات الله تعالى بل يجب كونها قائمة بذات الله تعالى. أنه فالذي يقوله المعتزلة من يجوز أن يكون الحي متكلما بكلام قائم بالغير حق وصدق، والذي يقوله أصحابنا أنه من يمتنع أن يكون الحي متكلما بكلام قائم بالغير حق وصدق، إلا أن الكلام الذي يشير إليه المعتزلة له معنى، والكلام الذي يشير إليه أصحابنا، له معنى آخر والفرقان لما لم يشتغلوا بتلخيص محل النزاع لا جرم خفيت هذه المباحث والمطالب.
And as for the third station: it is that we claim that this attribute is eternal, so we say: if it were temporal, it would either be subsisting in Him, or in another, or not in a locus. If it were subsisting in Him, then God Most High would be a locus for temporal events, and that is impossible. If it were subsisting in another, that is also impossible. And if it were not subsisting in anything, or if it were subsisting in another, or if it existed without a locus, then that is impossible. Because we have explained that this speech is an attribute and description of God Most High, and it is impossible for the attribute and description of a thing to occur not in it but in another. And what the Mu'tazila say, that it is permissible for His speech to subsist in something else, is this topic. Because they interpret speech subsisting in another as He creates sounds and letters that indicate by conventional placement that He Most High wills some things and dislikes some things, and this is not at all impossible. But as for us in this station, we have explained that if He created words indicating request and words indicating judgment and predication, then there must be meanings and concepts for those words, and we have explained that the words indicating request cannot have will as their meaning, and the words indicating news cannot have knowledge as their meaning, so there must be other attributes subsisting in the essence of God Most High, such that those attributes are the meanings of the words indicating request and the words indicating news. And those meanings cannot be separate from the essence of God Most High; rather, they must subsist in His essence. So what the Mu'tazila say—that it is permissible for the living being to speak with speech subsisting in another—is correct and truthful, and what our companions say—that it is impossible for the living being to speak with speech subsisting in another—is correct and truthful. Except that the speech that the Mu'tazila refer to has one meaning, and the speech that our companions refer to has another meaning. And because they did not engage in summarizing the subject of dispute, inevitably these investigations and demands remained hidden.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the eternality of God's speech (kalam). The author begins by stating the claim: this attribute (speech) is eternal. He then argues by disjunction: if it were temporal (hadith), it would have to be either subsisting in God (qaim bih), or in another, or not in a locus. Each possibility is refuted. If it subsists in God, then God would be a locus for temporal events (mahall li al-hawadith), which is impossible. If it subsists in another, that is also impossible because the attribute of a thing cannot subsist in another. If it is not in a locus, that is impossible as well. The author then discusses the Mu'tazila position, who claim that God's speech can subsist in another—e.g., created speech in the recorded text—by interpreting it as sounds and letters created by God that conventionally indicate His will or dislike. The author accepts that this is not impossible. Then he presents his own school's view: if God creates words that signify command or information, there must be meanings (madlulat) for those words. He argues that the meanings of command words cannot be will (irada) and the meanings of informational words cannot be knowledge ('ilm); therefore, there must be other attributes subsisting in God's essence. These meanings are the eternal speech. He concludes by clarifying that the Mu'tazila and the Asha'ira are talking about two different kinds of speech, and the dispute arises from not clearly defining the subject matter.

Key Terms
صفة قديمة
محدثة
قائمة به
قائمة بغيره
لا في محل
كلام
مدلول
المعتزلة
أصحابنا
إرادة
علم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that Razi rejects the possibility of created speech altogether.
Correction: Razi actually accepts created speech (sounds and letters) as possible, but he argues that there is also an eternal attribute of speech (the meaning) that subsists in God.

Checkpoint
According to Razi's argument in the third maqam, what is the first impossibility if God's speech were temporal?
A) It would subsist in another.
B) It would not be in a locus.
C) It would subsist in God, making Him a locus for temporal events.
D) It would be non-existent.

Key Takeaway
God's speech is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, distinct from any created sounds or letters that may indicate it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you recognize it as the eternal speech of God subsisting in His essence, or do you treat it as a mere temporal recitation? How does this belief change the weight of every verse you utter?
?
Razi insists that God's speech is not just sounds and letters but a real attribute in His essence. If God's speech is eternal and inseparable from Him, how should that reshape your sense of closeness to God when you hear or read His words? Are you truly encountering the eternal divine attribute, or just a created representation?
?
The Mu'tazila reduced God's speech to created signs of will and dislike. Are there areas in your life where you reduce God's attributes to mere symbols or intellectual concepts rather than living realities that demand your worship and transformation? What would it look like to let the eternal speech of God govern your heart today?

The Unity of God's Speech: All Commands and Prohibitions Are Khabar
Razi asserts God's speech is one, reducing command and prohibition to khabar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi argues that God's speech is one by reducing all commands and prohibitions to khabar (informative statements).

Core Idea
God's speech is one because command and prohibition are essentially informing the listener of reward and punishment.

Imam Razi tackles a key theological question: how can God's speech be one when it includes commands, prohibitions, and news? He resolves this by arguing that every command and prohibition is fundamentally an informative statement (khabar). This lesson unpacks his reasoning and its implications for understanding the divine attribute of speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the flow of Razi's argument. Note how he begins with the thesis that God's speech is one, then explains how command and prohibition are forms of khabar.
Pay attention to the definition of 'amr' and 'nahy' as informing about praise and blame.
2
Understand Razi's redefinition
Focus on how Razi redefines command and prohibition as types of informing (ta'rif). Compare this to the common assumption that they are distinct speech acts.
This redefinition is the key move to unify God's speech.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider why, if all speech is khabar, God's speech must be one. How does this argument fit into broader discussions of divine attributes?
Razi's approach shows that multiplicity in expression does not imply multiplicity in essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المقام الرابع : وهو أن كلام الله تعالى واحد، ومع كونه و كونه واحدًا فهو أمر ونهي وخبر، فتحقيق الكلام فيه يرجع إلى حرف واحد وهو أن الكلام كله خبر ؛ لأن الأمر عبارة عن تعريف الغير أنه لو فعله لصار مستحقا للمدح، ولو تركه لصار مستحقا للذم وكذا القول في النهي، وإذا كان المرجع بالكل إلى شيء واحد، وهو الخبر صح قولنا : إن كلام الله تعالى واحد فهذا مجموع ما نلخص في هذا الباب.
And as for the fourth station: it is that the speech of God Most High is one, and despite being one, it is command, prohibition, and news. So the verification of the matter returns to one point: that all speech is news. Because command is informing the other that if he does it, he becomes deserving of praise, and if he abandons it, he becomes deserving of blame. Similarly for prohibition. And since the reference of all is to one thing, which is news, our statement that God's speech is one is correct. This is the summary of what we have in this chapter.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the unity of God's speech. The author states that God's speech is one, yet it comprises command (amr), prohibition (nahy), and news (khabar). He resolves this apparent multiplicity by arguing that all speech is essentially khabar (informative statement). He defines command as informing (ta'rif) the listener that performing the action merits praise (madḥ) and avoiding it merits blame (dhamm). Prohibition is similarly defined as informing that avoiding the action merits praise and performing it merits blame. Therefore, command and prohibition are both types of khabar. Since the essence of all speech is informative, God's speech is one in reality.

Key Terms
واحد (one)
أمر (command)
نهي (prohibition)
خبر (news/information)
مدح (praise)
ذم (blame)
تعريف (informing)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think command and prohibition are fundamentally different from news and cannot be reduced.
Correction: Razi redefines them as types of informing: they inform the listener about what merits praise or blame, thus they are essentially khabar.

Checkpoint
How does Razi explain that command and prohibition are both essentially khabar?
A) They are both created.
B) They both inform the addressee about resulting praise or blame.
C) They both express God's will.
D) They are both eternal.

Key Takeaway
Razi's argument that command and prohibition are both forms of informing shows that God's speech, despite its diverse forms, is a single, unified attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's command is merely information about reward and punishment, do you treat it as urgent news that demands immediate action, or as a suggestion you can postpone? What would change if you truly believed that every command is a report about your eternal state?
?
Razi reduces command to informing about blame and praise. When you sin, do you feel the weight of God's 'news' about blame, or do you rationalize it away? How can you make yourself more sensitive to the khabar of your own actions?
?
Do you live as though God's speech is one unified truth, or do you pick and choose which parts to take seriously? Which command or prohibition have you compartmentalized as less important? Will you commit today to treating it as the same serious news as the rest?

The First Rational Objection: Eternal Command is Impossible
Razi presents the first rational objection against eternal command.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first rational objection against the eternity of the Quranic speech and its logical basis.

Core Idea
An eternal command addressed to no one is rationally absurd.

This lesson introduces the first rational objection raised by opponents of the Quran's eternity. The objection argues that if God's speech is eternal, it would involve commands and prohibitions directed at non-existent beings, which is considered foolishness. We will examine the objection's premises and its analogy with human speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Note that it begins by stating the impossibility of eternal command.
2
Identify the core argument
The objection claims that command and prohibition require the presence of the commanded and prohibited. Without them, it is foolishness.
The key is that an act of commanding is only rational if there is someone to command.
3
Analyze the analogy
Consider the analogy of a person speaking commands to an empty room, which is judged insane. How does this apply to God?
The analogy is meant to show the absurdity of eternal commands.
4
Extend to information
The objection also covers eternal information (khabar). If God is informing about things in pre-eternity, who is being informed? Futility or insanity.
5
Reflect on the objection's strength
Why does this objection seem compelling? It appeals to common sense about rational speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الشبه العقلية : فمن وجوه
الشبهة الأولى : أن الأمر سواء قلنا بأنه عبارة عن الحروف والأصوات أو قلنا : إنه معنى قائم بالنفس فإنه يمتنع أن يكون قديما، وذلك لأنه ما كان في الأزل مأمورًا ولا منهيًا، فلو حصل الأمر والنهي من غير حضور المأمور والمنهي كان هذا سفها وجنونًا، والدليل عليه أن الواحد منا لو جلس في بيته وحده، ويقول: يا زيد قم، ويا عمرو اجلس من غير أن يكون هناك أحد قضى كل عاقل بكونه مجنوناً، وما كان كذلك كيف يعقل إثباته في حق الله تعالى؟ وكيف يحسن في العقل أن يقول: ﴿يَا مُوسَى إِنِّي أَنَا رَبُّكَ فَاخْلَعْ نَعْلَيْكَ﴾ [طه] مع أنه لم يكن هناك موسى ولا أحد، وأيضًا لو كان تعالى مخبرًا في الأزل عن كيفيات الأشياء لكان ذلك الخبر إما أن يكون المقصود منه إخبار نفسه - وهو عبث - أو إخبار غيره أو لا يكون المقصود منه إخبار غيره، أما إخبار نفسه فهو عبث، وأما إخبار غيره مع أنه ليس هناك غيره فهو جنون وأما أن لا يكون المقصود منه لا هذا ولا ذلك، فهو محض العبث والسفه.
لا يقال: لو لا يجوز أن يقال : عن ذلك الأمر الأزلي كان أمرًا في الأزل للأشخاص الذين سيوجدون في لا يزال كما أنه تعالى كان قادرًا في الأزل على أن يوجد الخلق في لا يزال؟ وأيضًا أليس أن النبي كان يأمر وينهى حال حياته كل من سيوجد بعده إلى قيام القيامة، فثبت أن تقدم الأمر على المأمور غير ممتنع.
لأنا نقول : الأمر عبارة عن الطلب وتحقيق وجود الطلب مع أنه ليس هناك من يطلب منه شيء محال في العقول، بل العزم على الطلب قد يتقدم على الطلب، مثل أن الواحد منا إذا علم أنه سيوجد له ولد فإنه في الحال يعزم على أنه إذا وجد له ذلك الولد، فبعد وجوده يطلب منه تحصيل العلم والأدب، فأما أن يقال: إنه قبل وجود الولد يطلب منه تحصيل العلم والأدب، فهذا البتة غير معقول.
وأما قوله بأن النبي ﷺ كان يأمر حال حياته وينهى كل من يوجد بعده إلى قيام القيامة فنقول : هذه مغالطة، وذلك لأن النبي ﷺ ما كان له أمر ونهي على الخلق، بل هو له وكان يخبرنا أن أولئك الذين سيوجدون بعدي يحدث الله عليهم وجودهم وكمال عقلهم أنواعا من الأمر والنهي، وذلك الإخبار إنما حسن من الرسول لأنه حضر هناك من يسمع ذلك الخبر ويبلغه إلى الذين سيوجدون بعد ذلك، أما في الأزل فليس هناك أحد البتة يسمع ذلك الخبر، ويبلغه إلى الذين سيوجدون بعد ذلك، فظهر أن هذا المثال مغالطة محضة.
As for the rational objections, they are of several kinds. / The first objection: That the command, whether we say it consists of letters and sounds or we say it is a meaning subsisting in the soul, it is impossible that it be eternal. That is because in pre-eternity there was no one commanded nor prohibited. So if command and prohibition occurred without the presence of the commanded and the prohibited, this would be foolishness and insanity. The evidence for it is that if one of us sat alone in his house and said, 'O Zayd, stand!' and 'O Amr, sit!' while no one was there, every rational person would judge him to be insane. And if that is so, how can it rationally be attributed to Allah Almighty? And how is it rationally fitting that He say, 'O Moses, indeed I am your Lord, so take off your sandals' [Ta-Ha 20:12] while there was no Moses or anyone there? Also, if the Almighty were in pre-eternity informing about the qualities of things, that information would either be intended for informing Himself—which is futile—or for informing others, or for neither. Informing Himself is futile; informing others when there is no other is insanity; and intending neither is pure futility and foolishness. / It cannot be said: Why is it not permissible to say that that eternal command was a command in pre-eternity for persons who will come into existence in the future, just as the Almighty was powerful in pre-eternity to bring creation into existence in the future? Also, did not the Prophet command and forbid during his lifetime everyone who will come after him until the Day of Resurrection? So it is established that the precedence of the command over the commanded is not impossible. / But we say: The command is a request, and the actual existence of a request when there is no one from whom anything is requested is intellectually impossible. Rather, the resolve (al-azm) to request may precede the request, like when one of us knows that a child will be born to him; he then immediately resolves that when that child is born, after its existence he will request it to acquire knowledge and good manners. But as for saying that before the child exists he requests it to acquire knowledge and good manners—this is absolutely irrational. / As for the statement that the Prophet ﷺ used to command and forbid during his lifetime everyone who will come after him until the Day of Resurrection, we say: This is a sophistry. That is because the Prophet ﷺ did not have command and authority over those people; rather, he had it [in his lifetime] and he informed us that those who will come after me—Allah will create for them, upon their existence and completion of their intellect, types of command and prohibition. And that informing was good from the Messenger only because there were those present who heard that report and would convey it to those who would come later. As for pre-eternity, there was absolutely no one there to hear that report and convey it to those who would come later. So it becomes clear that this analogy is pure sophistry.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage presents the first rational objection (shubhah aqliyya) against the eternity of the Quran, followed by a detailed refutation. The objection argues that if God's speech (kalam) is eternal, then it would involve commands, prohibitions, and informatory statements addressed to no one, which is absurd. The author first distinguishes that command (amr) might be letters/sounds or a mental meaning, but in either case cannot be eternal because there were no commanded beings in pre-eternity. He uses the analogy of a person speaking orders to absent people, which is deemed insane. Then he anticipates a counterargument: just as God's power is eternal and applies to future creation, so His command could be eternal and apply to future beings. Also, the Prophet's commands addressed future generations. The author responds by distinguishing between a 'resolve' (azm) to command and an actual command. A resolve can precede, but an actual request directed at a non-existent being is irrational. As for the Prophet's example, he explains that the Prophet's commands were not directly addressed to future generations; rather, he informed his contemporaries, who would convey them. In pre-eternity, there was no audience. Thus the analogy fails. The author concludes that the objection is groundless.

Key Terms
شبهة عقلية
أمر
نهي
أزلي
مأمور
سفه
جنون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's speech must have a contemporaneous audience to be rational.
Correction: God's attributes are not bound by human limitations; His speech can be eternal without a current audience because it is a timeless attribute.

Checkpoint
Why does the objection consider an eternal command impossible?
A) Because it would be foolish
B) Because it requires a commanded person to exist at that time
C) Because God cannot speak
D) Because the Quran is created

Key Takeaway
The first rational objection argues that an eternal command is logically absurd because it lacks a recipient, making it similar to insane speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear rational objections to core Islamic beliefs, does your heart immediately seek to defend or does it waver? Write down a specific instance where you felt intellectually challenged by a theological question. How did you respond, and how can you strengthen your reliance on Allah's wisdom over your own reasoning?
?
The analogy of the person commanding alone highlights the absurdity of speech without a recipient. In your worship, are there actions you perform mindlessly, without heartfelt intention toward Allah? Choose one act of worship today and commit to performing it with full awareness that you are speaking to the All-Hearing, not to emptiness.

Refuting the Objection: The Nature of Eternal Command and Resolve
Razi refutes the first rational objection with two key responses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's refutation of the first rational objection, including the distinction between resolve and command.

Core Idea
An eternal command is not an actual request but a timeless attribute of will.

In the previous lesson we saw the objection. Now Razi provides a detailed refutation. He distinguishes between a resolve (azm) to command and the actual request, and he also explains why the Prophet's example does not apply. This lesson clarifies the intellectual foundations of the eternal speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation passage
Read the Arabic passage that begins with 'It cannot be said' and continues to the end.
2
Understand the counter-objection
The opponent uses the analogy of God's eternal power and the Prophet's commands to future generations to argue for the possibility of eternal command.
3
First response: Distinguish resolve from actual request
Razi argues that an actual request requires a present requester, but a resolve (azm) can precede. Example of a parent resolving to educate a future child.
4
Second response: Prophet analogy is a sophistry
The Prophet's commands were not directly to future people; he informed his companions who would convey them. In pre-eternity, no such audience exists.
5
Conclude the refutation
The objection fails because it confuses an eternal attribute with a temporal request, and the analogy is not analogous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الشبه العقلية : فمن وجوه
الشبهة الأولى : أن الأمر سواء قلنا بأنه عبارة عن الحروف والأصوات أو قلنا : إنه معنى قائم بالنفس فإنه يمتنع أن يكون قديما، وذلك لأنه ما كان في الأزل مأمورًا ولا منهيًا، فلو حصل الأمر والنهي من غير حضور المأمور والمنهي كان هذا سفها وجنونًا، والدليل عليه أن الواحد منا لو جلس في بيته وحده، ويقول: يا زيد قم، ويا عمرو اجلس من غير أن يكون هناك أحد قضى كل عاقل بكونه مجنوناً، وما كان كذلك كيف يعقل إثباته في حق الله تعالى؟ وكيف يحسن في العقل أن يقول: ﴿يَا مُوسَى إِنِّي أَنَا رَبُّكَ فَاخْلَعْ نَعْلَيْكَ﴾ [طه] مع أنه لم يكن هناك موسى ولا أحد، وأيضًا لو كان تعالى مخبرًا في الأزل عن كيفيات الأشياء لكان ذلك الخبر إما أن يكون المقصود منه إخبار نفسه - وهو عبث - أو إخبار غيره أو لا يكون المقصود منه إخبار غيره، أما إخبار نفسه فهو عبث، وأما إخبار غيره مع أنه ليس هناك غيره فهو جنون وأما أن لا يكون المقصود منه لا هذا ولا ذلك، فهو محض العبث والسفه.
لا يقال: لو لا يجوز أن يقال : عن ذلك الأمر الأزلي كان أمرًا في الأزل للأشخاص الذين سيوجدون في لا يزال كما أنه تعالى كان قادرًا في الأزل على أن يوجد الخلق في لا يزال؟ وأيضًا أليس أن النبي كان يأمر وينهى حال حياته كل من سيوجد بعده إلى قيام القيامة، فثبت أن تقدم الأمر على المأمور غير ممتنع.
لأنا نقول : الأمر عبارة عن الطلب وتحقيق وجود الطلب مع أنه ليس هناك من يطلب منه شيء محال في العقول، بل العزم على الطلب قد يتقدم على الطلب، مثل أن الواحد منا إذا علم أنه سيوجد له ولد فإنه في الحال يعزم على أنه إذا وجد له ذلك الولد، فبعد وجوده يطلب منه تحصيل العلم والأدب، فأما أن يقال: إنه قبل وجود الولد يطلب منه تحصيل العلم والأدب، فهذا البتة غير معقول.
وأما قوله بأن النبي ﷺ كان يأمر حال حياته وينهى كل من يوجد بعده إلى قيام القيامة فنقول : هذه مغالطة، وذلك لأن النبي ﷺ ما كان له أمر ونهي على الخلق، بل هو له وكان يخبرنا أن أولئك الذين سيوجدون بعدي يحدث الله عليهم وجودهم وكمال عقلهم أنواعا من الأمر والنهي، وذلك الإخبار إنما حسن من الرسول لأنه حضر هناك من يسمع ذلك الخبر ويبلغه إلى الذين سيوجدون بعد ذلك، أما في الأزل فليس هناك أحد البتة يسمع ذلك الخبر، ويبلغه إلى الذين سيوجدون بعد ذلك، فظهر أن هذا المثال مغالطة محضة.
As for the rational objections, they are of several kinds. / The first objection: That the command, whether we say it consists of letters and sounds or we say it is a meaning subsisting in the soul, it is impossible that it be eternal. That is because in pre-eternity there was no one commanded nor prohibited. So if command and prohibition occurred without the presence of the commanded and the prohibited, this would be foolishness and insanity. The evidence for it is that if one of us sat alone in his house and said, 'O Zayd, stand!' and 'O Amr, sit!' while no one was there, every rational person would judge him to be insane. And if that is so, how can it rationally be attributed to Allah Almighty? And how is it rationally fitting that He say, 'O Moses, indeed I am your Lord, so take off your sandals' [Ta-Ha 20:12] while there was no Moses or anyone there? Also, if the Almighty were in pre-eternity informing about the qualities of things, that information would either be intended for informing Himself—which is futile—or for informing others, or for neither. Informing Himself is futile; informing others when there is no other is insanity; and intending neither is pure futility and foolishness. / It cannot be said: Why is it not permissible to say that that eternal command was a command in pre-eternity for persons who will come into existence in the future, just as the Almighty was powerful in pre-eternity to bring creation into existence in the future? Also, did not the Prophet command and forbid during his lifetime everyone who will come after him until the Day of Resurrection? So it is established that the precedence of the command over the commanded is not impossible. / But we say: The command is a request, and the actual existence of a request when there is no one from whom anything is requested is intellectually impossible. Rather, the resolve (al-azm) to request may precede the request, like when one of us knows that a child will be born to him; he then immediately resolves that when that child is born, after its existence he will request it to acquire knowledge and good manners. But as for saying that before the child exists he requests it to acquire knowledge and good manners—this is absolutely irrational. / As for the statement that the Prophet ﷺ used to command and forbid during his lifetime everyone who will come after him until the Day of Resurrection, we say: This is a sophistry. That is because the Prophet ﷺ did not have command and authority over those people; rather, he had it [in his lifetime] and he informed us that those who will come after me—Allah will create for them, upon their existence and completion of their intellect, types of command and prohibition. And that informing was good from the Messenger only because there were those present who heard that report and would convey it to those who would come later. As for pre-eternity, there was absolutely no one there to hear that report and convey it to those who would come later. So it becomes clear that this analogy is pure sophistry.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage presents the first rational objection (shubhah aqliyya) against the eternity of the Quran, followed by a detailed refutation. The objection argues that if God's speech (kalam) is eternal, then it would involve commands, prohibitions, and informatory statements addressed to no one, which is absurd. The author first distinguishes that command (amr) might be letters/sounds or a mental meaning, but in either case cannot be eternal because there were no commanded beings in pre-eternity. He uses the analogy of a person speaking orders to absent people, which is deemed insane. Then he anticipates a counterargument: just as God's power is eternal and applies to future creation, so His command could be eternal and apply to future beings. Also, the Prophet's commands addressed future generations. The author responds by distinguishing between a 'resolve' (azm) to command and an actual command. A resolve can precede, but an actual request directed at a non-existent being is irrational. As for the Prophet's example, he explains that the Prophet's commands were not directly addressed to future generations; rather, he informed his contemporaries, who would convey them. In pre-eternity, there was no audience. Thus the analogy fails. The author concludes that the objection is groundless.

Key Terms
عزم
طلب
مغالطة
مأمور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An eternal command must be like a human verbal command issued in time.
Correction: God's eternal command is a timeless attribute of will (resolve), not an actual vocal request that requires a present audience.

Checkpoint
How does Razi refute the claim that eternal command is impossible?
A) By denying that God has command
B) By distinguishing between resolve and actual request
C) By saying the command is only metaphorical
D) By arguing that the Quran is created

Key Takeaway
Razi saves the eternity of command by distinguishing between a timeless attribute of will and a temporal request, and by showing that the Prophet analogy does not apply due to the absence of an audience in pre-eternity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God's 'command', do you unconsciously imagine it as a voice calling you? How does that reduce the Majesty of the One whose resolve is before time itself? Will you train your heart to submit to a command that precedes your existence?
?
Razi distinguishes between a request and a resolve. How often do you treat God's commands as mere suggestions rather than an irrevocable resolve? What would change in your life today if you truly believed His command is absolute?
?
The lesson argues that God's eternal command is a timeless attribute, not a temporal event. Are you living with the awareness that God's eternal resolve is already upon you, or do you only respond to temporal urgings? Commit to one action today that aligns with that eternal resolve.
